This workshop has been conducted in over ten different countries around the world with fantastic results aimed at both primary and secondary teachers. You can read more about these in some of the reviews we have received below.\nDale Sidebottom has been referred to as the energiser bunny of the PE world.                 "text": "National Disability Services (NDS) invites you to attend the Traralgon\u00a0Grant Designs\u00a0workshop. This workshop aims to help disability service providers, people with disability, carers and other stakeholders to learn to design projects in a way that will lead to strong disability workforce innovation and development proposals that meet the requirements of funders and the needs of current and future grant rounds.\nFacilitated by Workforce Connector Chris Hawken, the session will provide an opportunity for participants to explore project design using designated principles and best practice to assist and support their achievement of successful grant applications.\n\u00a0\nThe workshop will include:\n\nKnowledge and skills to articulate a project proposal using a structured design process and existing resources\nIncreased awareness and potentially inspiration from recent disability workforce innovations and previous projects that have applied or tested new workforce practices\nUnderstanding how to use the provided resources to address grant application criteria\nDevelopment of some ideas for a grant proposal to take back to their organisation for validation and refinement.\n\n\u00a0\nIt is advised that organisation representatives bring along their Mission and Vision statement and a laptop if possible to get the most out of the workshop.\n\u00a0\nThe session will provide:\nGrant Designs\u00a0workbook, Person-centred, Outcome Focussed Design (POPD) guide and other useful references.\n\u00a0\nAccessibility:\nThis venue is wheelchair accessible. Please contact the organiser directly with any additional accessibility requirements.\n\u00a0\nWho should attend?\nNDS recommends that most suited to attend include; CEOs, CFOs and HR Managers, Business Development Managers, Service providers large and small, people with disabilities, carers and relevant people from other disability workforce stakeholders.\n\u00a0\nEvent details:\n\u00a0\nDate:\u00a08 May 2019\nTime:\u00a09am \u2013 5pm\nLocation:\u00a0Century Inn, 5 Airfield Rd Traralgon\nCost:\u00a0Free",

It evaluates the set of skills that define how effectively people perceive, understand, reason with and manage their own feelings and the feelings of others around them, enabling them to be more socially aware and confident to build stronger business relationships.\r\n\u00a0\r\nLearning outcomes\r\nFollowing the program, participants will:\r\n\r\nUnderstand the concept of emotional intelligence and it\u2019s workplace application\r\nHave improved personal awareness and insight into their own behaviour\r\nBe able to effectively apply techniques to manage and control personal emotional reactions to situations at work\r\nFoster positive workplace relationships and empathise, understand and communicate better with others\r\nMotivate and influence others to perform\r\nRecognise how Emotional Intelligence can improve workplace decision making\r\nKnow how to manage their own emotions and the emotions of others\r\nFoster a more positive environment which supports the development of sustainable workplace relationships\r\n\r\nMethodology\r\nThis program is highly interactive with a high degree of reflection and action planning to assist participant\u2019s to turn their learning into habits.\u00a0 We focus on skills and tools to use back in the workplace.\r\nProgram details\r\nFormat:\u00a0Full Day\r\nDate:\u00a0 Wednesday 8th May 2019\u00a0\r\nTime:\u00a09.00am - 4.00pm\r\nLocation:\u00a0 Kooyong Lawn Tennis Club, 489 Glenferrie Rd, Kooyong VIC 3144\u00a0\r\nContact:\u00a01300t2talk or info@time2talk.com.au",

                "text": "What do thesis examiners really want?\nDoes a thesis have an audience of 2 or 2000? While you write for other researchers in your field, you must first please just two people: your examiners. In this workshop, we will examine the research on how examiners examine and ask: What separates a good thesis from a bad one? Why do examiners look for their own work in the bibliography? What makes examiners cranky? And other burning questions.\nBy the end of this workshop you will:\n\nHave a better understanding of the examination process generally and how it tends to work at ANU.\nKnow what the 'pain points' for examiners are and how to plan for them in the way you write your thesis.\nHave started developing an examiner selection template.\n\nThis workshop will be presented by\u00a0Dr Cally Guerin, a Learning Advisor in Research Skills and Training at The Australian National University. She has worked in researcher education since 2008. Her research interests include research writing, academic identities, the academic workforce, and doctoral education. She is a founding co-editor of the DoctoralWriting blog. Cally is a Senior Fellow of the Higher Education Academy (now known as Advance HE).                 "text": "Law for Non-Lawyers\nLegal Aid ACT, Community Legal Centres, and other organisations are delivering a range of legal training sessions from February to June 2019.\nFollowing, are details about each session that will be delivered between February-June. Each session will be held on a Wednesday morning, at the same time, and in the same location.\u00a0\nTime:\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0 9.30am to 11.30am\nLocation:\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0 Legal Aid, 2 Allsop Street, Canberra City\nCost:\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0 FREE. Materials and morning tea included\n\n\nIf you have questions about the training email: community.education@legalaidact.org.au\nYou are welcome to attend any or all of the sessions.\nPlease tell us your participation needs.\n\n\nWednesday 20 February \u2013 How to Spot a Legal Issue \nLegal problems are pervasive and impact on many aspects of people\u2019s lives. Unaddressed legal problems can quickly escalate and may cause other problems as well. Early identification and action are key to ensuring legal problems do not get out of control.\nThis session will cover:\n\n\nHow to identify the sorts of problems in life that may be capable of a legal solution\n\n\nProvide some examples of positive outcomes that can be achieved with legal assistance\n\n\nProvide an example of a \u2018legal health check\u2019 which can quickly and easily identify common legal problems\n\n\nOutline what makes an effective referral to legal services, including the sort of information it is helpful to include in a referral\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by a lawyer from Street Law, an outreach legal service for people experiencing or at risk of homelessness.\n\n\nWednesday 6 March \u2013 The Australian Legal System and Visa Issues\nThe Australian Migration system can be very confusing and difficult to understand. When problems do arise with visas, it can affect every aspect of a person\u2019s life in Australia and can leave people very vulnerable.\nThis session will provide a broad overview of the migration system to help community and frontline workers better understand the problems clients on visas may be facing. It will also identify common areas where visa issues can arise and how clients can seek help. This session is part of the\u00a0Law for Non-Lawyers series and Migration Matters series.\u00a0\nThis session will cover:\n\n\nBasic overview of the Australian Migration System\n\n\nKey terminology\n\n\nVisas and employment issues\n\n\nVisas and family violence\n\n\nVisa cancellations focusing on detainees\n\n\nGetting legal advice\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by Er-Kai Wang, Associate Lecturer at the ANU College of Law.\n\n\nWednesday 27 March \u2013 Elder Law\nOlder people may experience a range of legal problems including elder abuse and problematic financial arrangements with family members, which can increase their vulnerability. The Older Persons ACT Legal Service, a specialist service within Legal Aid ACT, can provide legal advice and assistance to older people in the ACT.\nThis session will cover:\n\n\nOverview of Enduring Powers of Attorney\n\n\nFinancial arrangements with family members\n\n\nElder Abuse\n\n\nThis session will be delivered jointly by lawyers from Legal Aid ACT\u2019s Older Persons ACT Legal Service (OPALS) and the Consumer Law Centre.\n\n\nWednesday 10 April \u2013 Young People and the Law\nThere are many legal issues faced by young people in the ACT. The Youth Law Centre assists hundreds of young people each year deal with assorted legal issues. This session will look at some of the main issues faced by young people and the ways the Youth Law Centre can assist.\nThis session will cover:\n\n\nDriving issues\n\n\nEmployment problems\n\n\nFamily court orders\n\n\nHomelessness\n\n\nMobile Phones\n\n\nSchool issues\n\n\nBasic differences of the Youth Criminal Justice System\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by the Youth Law Centre ACT.\n\n\n Wednesday 8 May \u2013 Child and Youth Protection Services\nChild and Youth Protection Services (CYPS) has a statutory responsibility to support children, young people and families requiring a care or justice response. In doing so, CYPS works to deliver good client outcomes through providing a response that focuses on the following areas, this session will cover these areas and the work of CYPs.\n\n\nDiversion\n\n\nProtection\n\n\nRestoration\n\n\nTransition and Permanency\n\n\nTrauma Informed Practice\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by Child & Youth Protection Services.\n\n\nWednesday 22 May \u2013 Employment Law 101\nThis session is designed to give community and frontline workers an understanding of the Australian employment framework.\nIt will cover:\n\n\nEmployment relationships\n\n\nApplicable laws\n\n\nEmployment standards\n\n\nUnfair dismissal\n\n\nGeneral Protections\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by a lawyer from the Women\u2019s Legal Centre.\n\n\nWednesday 12 June \u2013 Family Law 101\nThis session will cover the basics of family law and provide an understanding of the Family Law Act 1975.\nThis session will cover the following topics:\n\n\nOverview of the Family Law system\n\n\nSeparation and divorce\n\n\nChildren\n\n\nProperty\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by a lawyer from the Women\u2019s Legal Centre.\n\n\nWednesday 26 June \u2013 Housing\nThis session will focus on public housing in the ACT.\nIt will include:\n\n\nOverview of the application process\n\n\nEligibility issues including for priority housing\n\n\nDebts that may arise as a result of tenants responsible maintenance or rent arrears\n\n\nWhat happens when clients are seeking a transfer to another Housing ACT property\n\n\nIssues that commonly lead to Housing ACT making an application to the ACT Civil and Administrative Tribunal for the termination of the tenancy\n\n\nThis session will be delivered by a lawyer from Canberra Community Law.\n \u00a0\n\n\n\u00a0",

                "text": "Council Planner Forums\n\nSessions are scheduled for five regional Victorian locations:\n\nDepartment of Environment, Land, Water and Planning (DELWP) and Environment Protection Authority Victoria (EPA) are holding a series of professional development forums for planners and other local government staff to update you on the delivery of the Government\u2019s environment protection reform agenda, to demonstrate new data tools and to seek feedback on key planning reform projects.\nThe Planning Minister, Richard Wynne, gazetted Ministerial Direction 19 in Ocober 2018. Planning Authorities are now required to seek the advice of the EPA when undertaking a range of strategic planning activities and include this advice\u00a0with their application for authorisation to prepare a planning scheme amendment. \u200bIn this forum we will review what matters should be referred to EPA and explain the process. \nThe New Environment Protection Act, 2017 is coming into force on 1 July 2020. It involves changes to EPA subordinate legislations and strengthening EPA\u2019s role in land use planning. A key change is a new preventative environmental duty which Councils will need to comply with. We will provide a preliminary overview of the new Act and discuss implications for local government. \nTo find out how these changes might affect your planning assessment process you are invited to attend one of the scheduled sessions and receive information about:\n\nMinisterial Direction 19 and Ministerial Requirement for Planning Authorities\nthe new Environment Protection Act 2017 and development of subordinate instruments / consequential changes underway in respect to making informed and effective planning assessments and decisions\nnew planning guidance being prepared by EPA Victoria\nthe new Windfarm Noise Amendment and its effects on the planning assessment process\nthe status of EPA's transformation and the environment protection reform agenda\nVicUnearthed Database and Preliminary Risk Screening Pilot Projects - two new initiatives designed to assist councils and other landholders to better manage contaminated or potentially contaminated land.\n\n** Light lunch is included.\nRegistrations are essential.\nPlease contact our team if you have any further enquiries about the sessions, via email to stratplan@epa.vic.gov.au\nSessions that have previously been held:\nMetro West \u2013 Tuesday 26 February - Sunshine\nMetro Southeast \u2013 Friday 1 March - Dandenong\nMetro Central \u2013 Monday 4 March - Melbourne CBD\nRegional North\u00a0\u2013 Tuesday 19 March - Bendigo\nRegional Northeast\u00a0\u2013\u00a0Tuesday 26 March -\u00a0Wangaratta\nRegional Northwest\u00a0\u2013 Thursday 28 March - Mildura\nRegional Southeast\u00a0\u2013 Tuesday, 2 April - Traralgon\nRegional Southwest\u00a0\u2013 Tuesday, 9 April -\u00a0Warrnambool",

                "text": "Whether your business is in a growth phase or you have a potential exit on the horizon, effective succession planning can make or break your strategy.\u00a0\u00a0\nConnecting to the right support networks can help you close the knowledge gap between where you are today and where you want to be in the future.\nWhat would it mean for your business if you could call upon the experience of other entrepreneurs, CEOs,\u00a0 technical experts, innovators and disruptors to help you make the right decisions about the direction you\u2019re taking\u2014not self-professed online \u2018gurus\u2019 but reputable experts who take the time to know your business and who care about your success?\nAn advisory board is an effective way to benefit from genuine support and insight to accelerate your strategy and give your business a competitive edge.\nYour advisory board can connect you to bigger networks and expertise that you might not have on your operational team \u2013 like how to manage the challenges and opportunities of business growth or exit.\n\nLouise Broekman, successful business owner and founder of the Advisory Board Centre will\u00a0be facilitating this executive roundtable session.\u00a0 Participants are invited to discover:\n\n\nThe \"Make or Break\" points of business growth and exit considerations\n\n\nHow to engage effectively with Advisors to support your business\n\n\nThe benefits of a formalised advisory board; and\n\n\nThe factors to consider when setting up an advisory board.\n\n\n\nLouise will facilitate a panel discussion and open Q&A session featuring\u00a0Rod Naismith, Partner at BDO.\u00a0 In his role at BDO, Rob provides advice on a\u00a0broad range of business, tax and accounting issues impacting growing, dynamic businesses and their owners.\u00a0\nThe Executive Roundtable is held in a boardroom format with numbers strictly limited to ensure a high standard of engagement.                 "text": "Tai Chi and Qigong Classes in MentoneTai Chi (Taijiquan in Chinese) is literally an internal Chinese Martial Art that has been practiced in China since the 16th Century.
